For FT-1, we exposed three rock samples with different saturation regimes (30%, 70%, 100%) to 20 freeze-thaw cycles between 10 and -10Â°C while monitoring rock temperature and acoustic emission (AE). We scanned the rock samples using micro computational tomography (CT) before the first cycle, after 5, 10, 15 and 20 cycles. For FT-2, we exposed three rock samples with different saturation regimes (30%, 70%, 100%) to one sustained freezing cycle with 66 h freezing at -10Â°C while monitoring rock temperature and AE.  We scanned the rock samples using micro CT before the first cycle and after the end of the experiment. The data set comprises all micro CT scans, rock temperature and AE data.",

                "msl_citation": "Muscarella, L. A., &amp; Jöbsis, H. J. (2023). <i>Which Ion Dominates Temperature and Pressure Response of Halide Perovskites and Elpasolites?</i> (Version 1.0) [Data set]. Utrecht University. https://doi.org/10.24416/UU01-W60H58",
                "msl_datacite_version": "1.0",
                "msl_description_abstract": "Halide perovskite and elpasolite semiconductors are extensively studied for optoelectronic applications due to their excellent performance together with significant chemical and structural flexibility. However, there is still limited understanding of how their basic elastic properties vary with crystal orientation, composition and temperature, which is relevant for synthesis and device operation. To address this, we performed temperature- and pressure-dependent synchrotron-based powder X-ray diffraction (XRD). In contrast to previous pressure-dependent XRD studies, our relatively low pressures (ambient to 0.06 GPa) enabled us to investigate the elastic properties of halide perovskites and elpasolites in their ambient crystal structure. We find that halide perovskites and elpasolites show common trends in the bulk modulus and thermal expansivity. Both materials become softer as the halide ionic radius increases from Cl to Br to I, exhibiting higher compressibility and larger thermal expansivity. The mixed-halide compositions show intermediate properties to the pure compounds. Contrary, cations show a minor effect on the elastic properties. Finally, we observe that thermal phase transitions in e.g., MAPbI3 and CsPbCl3 lead to a softening of the lattice, together with negative expansivity for certain crystal axes, already tens of degrees away from the transition temperature. Hence, the range in which the phase transition affects thermal and elastic properties is substantially broader than previously thought. These findings highlight the importance of considering the temperature-dependent elastic properties of these materials, since stress induced during manufacturing or temperature sweeps can significantly impact the stability and performance of the corresponding devices. ",
                "msl_description_abstract_annotated": "Halide <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/materials/1.3/minerals-oxide_mineral-perovskite\"]'>perovskite</span> and elpasolite semiconductors are extensively studied for optoelectronic applications due to their excellent performance together with significant chemical and structural flexibility. To address this, we performed temperature- and pressure-dependent synchrotron-based powder <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/microscopy/1.3/technique-imaging_3d-computed_tomography_ct-x-ray_diffraction\"]'>X-ray diffraction</span> (<span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/microscopy/1.3/technique-imaging_3d-computed_tomography_ct-x-ray_diffraction\"]'>XRD</span>). In contrast to previous pressure-dependent <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/microscopy/1.3/technique-imaging_3d-computed_tomography_ct-x-ray_diffraction\"]'>XRD</span> studies, our relatively low pressures (ambient to 0.06 GPa) enabled us to investigate the elastic properties of halide perovskites and elpasolites in their ambient crystal structure. Both materials become softer as the halide ionic radius increases from Cl to Br to I, exhibiting higher <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/rockphysics/1.3/measured_property-elasticity-axial_compressibility\", \"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/rockphysics/1.3/measured_property-elasticity-bulk_compressibility\"]'>compressibility</span> and larger thermal expansivity. The mixed-halide compositions show intermediate properties to the pure compounds. Contrary, cations show a minor effect on the elastic properties. Finally, we observe that thermal phase transitions in e.g., MAPbI3 and CsPbCl3 lead to a softening of the lattice, together with negative expansivity for certain crystal axes, already tens of degrees away from the transition temperature. Hence, the range in which the phase transition affects thermal and elastic properties is substantially broader than previously thought. These findings highlight the importance of considering the temperature-dependent elastic properties of these materials, since stress induced during manufacturing or temperature sweeps can significantly impact the stability and performance of the corresponding devices.                 "msl_datacite_version": "1.0",
                "msl_description_abstract": "This data package contains all the reconstructed µCT scans that were analyzed and displayed in the publication from Schröer et al. titled 3D Visualization of Cyanobacterial Biofilms using Micro-Computed Tomography with Contrast-Enhancing Staining Agents. The goal of this research and this data was to visualize cyanobacterial biofilms using micro-computed tomography using five different contras-enhancing staining agents (CESAs)\nEvery folder contains a series of .tiff files making up a 3D volume and a text file that describes either the scanning or reconstruction parameters. The µCT scans show six samples of biofilms of Phormidium autumnale ULC086 colonizing Bentheim sandstone. The biofilms were stained with (1) Isotonic Lugol, (2) Hexabrix, (3) Mono-WD POM, (4) Hf-WD 1:2 POM, (5) CA4+ or remained (6) blank as control.\n\nThe data is provided in six subfolders. Detailed information about the files in these subfolders is given in the explanatory file ReadMe_3dcyano.txt. Contact person is Laurenz Schröer - laurenz.schroer@ugent.be",
                "msl_description_abstract_annotated": "This data package contains all the reconstructed µ<span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/microscopy/1.3/apparatus-x-ray_tomography\"]'>CT scans</span> that were analyzed and displayed in the publication from Schröer et al. titled 3D Visualization of Cyanobacterial Biofilms using Micro-<span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/microscopy/1.3/technique-imaging_3d-computed_tomography_ct\"]'>Computed Tomography</span> with Contrast-Enhancing Staining Agents. The goal of this research and this data was to visualize cyanobacterial biofilms using micro-<span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/microscopy/1.3/technique-imaging_3d-computed_tomography_ct\"]'>computed tomography</span> using five different contras-enhancing staining agents (CESAs)\nEvery folder contains a series of .tiff files making up a 3D volume and a text file that describes either the scanning or reconstruction parameters. The µ<span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/microscopy/1.3/apparatus-x-ray_tomography\"]'>CT scans</span> show six samples of biofilms of Phormidium autumnale ULC086 colonizing <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/materials/1.3/sedimentary_rock-sandstone-arenite-bentheim_sandstone\"]'>Bentheim sandstone</span>. The biofilms were stained with (1) Isotonic Lugol, (2) Hexabrix, (3) Mono-WD POM, (4) Hf-WD 1:2 POM, (5) CA4+ or remained (6) blank as control.\n\nThe data is provided in six subfolders. Detailed information about the files in these subfolders is given in the explanatory file ReadMe_3dcyano.txt. Contact person is Laurenz Schröer - laurenz.schroer@ugent.be",

                "msl_citation": "Govers, R. M. A. (2021). Data supplement of \"Tectonic context and possible triggering of the 2019-2020 Puerto Rico earthquake sequence\". <i>Utrecht University</i>. https://doi.org/10.24416/UU01-I5E13S",
                "msl_datacite_version": "1.0",
                "msl_description_abstract": "Paper Abstract: An historically unprecedented seismic moment was released by crustal events of the 2019-2020 earthquake sequence near southwest Puerto Rico. The sequence involved at least two, and per-haps three interacting fault systems. The largest Mw 6.4 event was likely triggered by left lateral strike-slip events along the eastern extension of the North Boquerón Bay-Punta Montalva fault zone. The mainshock occurred in a normal fault zone that extends into a region where previous studies documented extensional deformation, beyond the Ponce fault and the Bajo Tasmanian fault. Coulomb stress changes by the mainshock may have triggered further normal faulting af-tershocks, left lateral strike-slip events in the region where these two fault zones interacted, and possibly right lateral strike-slip aftershocks along a third structure extending southward, the Guayanilla fault zone. Extension directions of the seismic sequence are consistently NNW-SSE oriented, in agreement with the GNSS-inferred motion direction of eastern Hispaniola relative to western Puerto Rico, and with crustal stress estimates for the overriding plate boundary zone.\n\nData in this repository was used for the figures and as input data for Coulomb stress modeling. The software for making the figures was Generic Mapping Tools (Wessel et al., 2019). The software for computing coseismic stress changes is available online (https://doi.org/10.5281/zenodo.3894137).\n\nThe data is provided in the main folder and 2 subfolders. Detailed information about these files as well as information on how the data is processed is given in the explanatory file readme.txt. Contact person is Dr Rob Govers - r.govers@uu.nl.\n\n",
                "msl_description_abstract_annotated": "Paper Abstract: An historically unprecedented seismic moment was released by <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/geologicalsetting/1.3/earths_structure-earth_crust\"]'>crustal</span> events of the 2019-2020 earthquake sequence near southwest Puerto Rico. The sequence involved at least two, and per-haps three interacting fault systems. The largest Mw 6.4 event was likely triggered by left lateral strike-slip events along the eastern extension of the North Boquerón Bay-Punta Montalva <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/geologicalsetting/1.3/tectonic_deformation_structure-tectonic_fault\"]'>fault zone</span>. The mainshock occurred in a <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/geologicalsetting/1.3/tectonic_deformation_structure-tectonic_fault-normal_fault\"]'>normal fault</<span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/geologicalsetting/1.3/tectonic_deformation_structure-tectonic_fault\"]'>span> zone</span> that extends into a region where previous studies documented extensional deformation, beyond the Ponce fault and the Bajo Tasmanian fault. <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/rockphysics/1.3/inferred_deformation_behavior-deformation_behaviour-brittle_deformation\"]'>Coulomb</span> stress changes by the mainshock may have triggered further <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/geologicalsetting/1.3/tectonic_deformation_structure-tectonic_fault-normal_fault\"]'>normal faulting</span> af-tershocks, left lateral strike-slip events in the region where these two <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/geologicalsetting/1.3/tectonic_deformation_structure-tectonic_fault\"]'>fault zones</span> interacted, and possibly right lateral strike-slip aftershocks along a third structure extending southward, the Guayanilla <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/geologicalsetting/1.3/tectonic_deformation_structure-tectonic_fault\"]'>fault zone</span>. Extension directions of the seismic sequence are consistently NNW-SSE oriented, in agreement with the GNSS-inferred motion direction of eastern Hispaniola relative to western Puerto Rico, and with <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/geologicalsetting/1.3/earths_structure-earth_crust\"]'>crustal</span> stress estimates for the overriding plate boundary zone.\n\nData in this repository was used for the figures and as input data for <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/rockphysics/1.3/inferred_deformation_behavior-deformation_behaviour-brittle_deformation\"]'>Coulomb</span> stress modeling. The software for making the figures was Generic Mapping Tools (Wessel et al., 2019). The software for computing coseismic stress changes is available online (https://doi.org/10.5281/zenodo.3894137).\n\nThe data is provided in the main folder and 2 subfolders. Detailed information about these files as well as information on how the data is processed is given in the explanatory file readme.txt. Contact person is Dr Rob Govers - r.govers@uu.nl.\n\n",

                "msl_datacite_version": "Version 1.0",
                "msl_description_abstract": "We performed friction experiments on simulated basaltic gouge under hydrothermal conditions to investigate roles of subducting oceanic crust on seismogenesis in subduction zones. In this dataset, we report raw data, processed data after removal of seal friction effects, velocity dependence of friction coefficients, and the processing script for each experiment.\n\nThe data is provided in 13 zip-files for 13 experiments. Detailed information about the files in these zip-files as well as information on how the data is processed is given in the explanatory file Okuda-et-al-2022-Data-Description.pdf.\n\nA new version of this data package has been published and can been found here: https://public.yoda.uu.nl/geo/UU01/Q0VVEX.html",

                "msl_citation": "Brückner, M. Z. M. (2021). <i>Model files for the benthic species model</i> (Version 1.0) [Data set]. Utrecht University. https://doi.org/10.24416/UU01-GWLKT8",
                "msl_datacite_version": "1.0",
                "msl_description_abstract": "This repository includes the model files used in the publication of Brückner et al. 2021 - \"Benthic species as mud patrol‐modelled effects of bioturbators and biofilms on large‐scale estuarine mud and morphology\" doi: https://doi.org/10.1002/esp.5080.\nThe files contain the initial model domain used in the Delft3D model and the associated Delft3D files. More information about the data and its content can be found in readme.txt. Contact person is Muriel Brückner - Researcher - M.Bruckner@exeter.ac.uk.\n\nAbstract study: \n\nSediment-stabilizing and -destabilizing organisms, i.e. microphytobenthos (biofilms) and macrozoobenthos (bioturbators), affect the erodibility of muddy sediments, potentially altering large-scale estuarine morphology. Using a novel eco-morphodynamic model of an idealized estuary, we investigate eco-engineering effects of microphytobenthos and two macrozoobenthic bioturbators. Local mud erodibility is based on species pattern predicted through hydrodynamics, soil mud content, competition and grazing.\n\nMud resuspension and export is enhanced under bioturbation and prevented under biostabilization through respective exposure and protection of the supra- and intertidal. Bioturbation decreases mud thickness and bed elevations, which increases net mud fluxes. Microphytobenthos reduces erosion, leading to a local mud increase of intertidal sediments.\n\nIn multi-species scenarios, an effective mud-prone bioturbator strongly alters morphology, exceeding that of a more abundant sand-prone moderate species, showing that morphological change depends on species traits as opposed to abundance. Altering their habitat, the effective mud-prone bioturbator facilitates expansion of the sand-prone moderate bioturbator. Grazing and species competition favor species distributions of dominant bioturbators. Consequently, eco-engineering affects habitat conditions while species interactions determine species dominance.\n\nOur results show that eco-engineering species determine the mud content of the estuary, which suggests large effects on the morphology of estuaries with aggravating habitat degradation.\n",
                "msl_description_abstract_annotated": "This repository includes the model files used in the publication of Brückner et al. 2021 - \"Benthic species as <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/materials/1.3/unconsolidated_sediment-clastic_sediment-mud\"]'>mud</span> patrol‐modelled effects of bioturbators and biofilms on large‐scale estuarine <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/materials/1.3/unconsolidated_sediment-clastic_sediment-mud\"]'>mud</span> and morphology\" doi: https://doi.org/10.1002/esp.5080.\nThe files contain the initial model domain used in the Delft3D model and the associated Delft3D files. More information about the data and its content can be found in readme.txt. Contact person is Muriel Brückner - Researcher - M.Bruckner@exeter.ac.uk.\n\nAbstract study: \n\nSediment-stabilizing and -destabilizing organisms, i.e. microphytobenthos (biofilms) and macrozoobenthos (bioturbators), affect the <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/analoguemodelling/1.3/measured_property-mechanical_strength-erodibility\", \"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/analoguemodelling/1.3/measured_property-geomorphic_evolution-erodibility\"]'>erodibility</span> of muddy sediments, potentially altering large-scale estuarine morphology. Using a novel eco-morphodynamic model of an idealized estuary, we investigate eco-engineering effects of microphytobenthos and two macrozoobenthic bioturbators. Local <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/materials/1.3/unconsolidated_sediment-clastic_sediment-mud\"]'>mud</span> <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/analoguemodelling/1.3/measured_property-mechanical_strength-erodibility\", \"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/analoguemodelling/1.3/measured_property-geomorphic_evolution-erodibility\"]'>erodibility</span> is based on species pattern predicted through hydrodynamics, soil <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/materials/1.3/unconsolidated_sediment-clastic_sediment-mud\"]'>mud</span> content, competition and grazing.\n\n<span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/materials/1.3/unconsolidated_sediment-clastic_sediment-mud\"]'>Mud</span> resuspension and export is enhanced under bioturbation and prevented under biostabilization through respective exposure and protection of the supra- and intertidal. Bioturbation decreases <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/materials/1.3/unconsolidated_sediment-clastic_sediment-mud\"]'>mud</span> thickness and bed elevations, which increases net <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/materials/1.3/unconsolidated_sediment-clastic_sediment-mud\"]'>mud</span> fluxes. Microphytobenthos reduces erosion, leading to a local <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/materials/1.3/unconsolidated_sediment-clastic_sediment-mud\"]'>mud</span> increase of intertidal sediments.\n\nIn multi-species scenarios, an effective <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/materials/1.3/unconsolidated_sediment-clastic_sediment-mud\"]'>mud</span>-prone bioturbator strongly alters morphology, exceeding that of a more abundant <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/materials/1.3/unconsolidated_sediment-clastic_sediment-sand\"]'>sand</span>-prone moderate species, showing that morphological change depends on species traits as opposed to abundance. Altering their habitat, the effective <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/materials/1.3/unconsolidated_sediment-clastic_sediment-mud\"]'>mud</span>-prone bioturbator facilitates expansion of the <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/materials/1.3/unconsolidated_sediment-clastic_sediment-sand\"]'>sand</span>-prone moderate bioturbator. Grazing and species competition favor species distributions of dominant bioturbators. Consequently, eco-engineering affects habitat conditions while species interactions determine species dominance.\n\nOur results show that eco-engineering species determine the <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/materials/1.3/unconsolidated_sediment-clastic_sediment-mud\"]'>mud</span> content of the estuary, which suggests large effects on the morphology of estuaries with aggravating habitat degradation.\n",

                "msl_citation": "Kopacz, N. (2022). <i>Data supplement to \"A Study in Blue: Secondary Copper-rich Minerals and their Associated Bacterial Diversity in Icelandic Lava Tubes\"</i> (Version 1.0) [Data set]. Utrecht University. https://doi.org/10.24416/UU01-I32Z95",
                "msl_datacite_version": "1.0",
                "msl_description_abstract": "Lava tubes on Earth represent some of the most enticing Martian analogue environments when investigating the possibility of past or present life on Mars. Lava tubes provide stable, sheltered environments, isolated and protected from the radiation on the surface. The microbial mats in these caves further regulate the environment for life, allowing various microbial communities with different metabolisms to coexist. This adaptation is so successful, one could imagine such a microbe-mineral continuum might occur on other planets. The data from this package is from investigated lava caves in Iceland. The project aims to correlate biological and mineralogical data to describe the interactions between the microbes and their geological substrates, to identify microbe-specific speleothems as biosignatures, and to develop a sampling technique in these fragile environments. This is achieved with a combination of X-ray fluorescence spectroscopy (XRF), DNA sequencing, scanning electron microscopy coupled with energy-dispersive X-ray spectroscopy (SEM/EDS), and confocal Raman microscopy.\n\nThe data is provided in 6 subfolders for 6 experiments/samples. Detailed information about the files in these subfolders is given in the explanatory file Kopacz_et_al_2022_Data_description. Contact person is Nina Kopacz - Researcher - k.a.kopacz@uu.nl",
                "msl_description_abstract_annotated": "<span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/materials/1.3/igneous_rock_-_extrusive-lava\"]'>Lava</span> tubes on Earth represent some of the most enticing Martian analogue environments when investigating the possibility of past or present life on Mars. <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/materials/1.3/igneous_rock_-_extrusive-lava\"]'>Lava</span> tubes provide stable, sheltered environments, isolated and protected from the radiation on the surface. The microbial mats in these caves further regulate the environment for life, allowing various microbial communities with different metabolisms to coexist. This adaptation is so successful, one could imagine such a microbe-mineral continuum might occur on other planets. The data from this package is from investigated <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/materials/1.3/igneous_rock_-_extrusive-lava\"]'>lava</span> caves in Iceland. The project aims to correlate biological and mineralogical data to describe the interactions between the microbes and their geological substrates, to identify microbe-specific speleothems as biosignatures, and to develop a sampling technique in these fragile environments. This is achieved with a combination of <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/geochemistry/1.3/equipment-x-ray_spectrometer-x-ray_fluorescence_spectrometer\"]'>X-ray fluorescence</span> spectroscopy (<span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/geochemistry/1.3/equipment-x-ray_spectrometer-x-ray_fluorescence_spectrometer\"]'>XRF</span>), DNA sequencing, scanning <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/microscopy/1.3/apparatus-electron_microscopy\"]'>electron microscopy</span> coupled with energy-dispersive <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/geochemistry/1.3/equipment-x-ray_spectrometer\"]'>X-ray spectroscopy</span> (SEM/<span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/geochemistry/1.3/equipment-x-ray_spectrometer-energy-dispersive_x-ray_spectrometer\"]'>EDS</span>), and confocal <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/microscopy/1.3/technique-chemical_and_mineralogical_analysis-raman_spectrometry_-_chemistry_and_mineralogy\", \"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/microscopy/1.3/technique-crystal_structure_analysis-raman_spectrometry_-_crystal_lattice\"]'>Raman</span> microscopy.\n\nThe data is provided in 6 subfolders for 6 experiments/samples. Detailed information about the files in these subfolders is given in the explanatory file Kopacz_et_al_2022_Data_description. Contact person is Nina Kopacz - Researcher - k.a.kopacz@uu.nl",

                "author": null,
                "author_email": null,
                "creator_user_id": "ff0afeb5-e2da-4683-a54d-8ff1a20585e0",
                "id": "b5f2e9e0-1949-43ab-b792-f907b40e3e5c",
                "isopen": false,
                "license_id": null,
                "license_title": null,
                "maintainer": null,
                "maintainer_email": null,
                "metadata_created": "2025-06-20T15:06:08.257045",
                "metadata_modified": "2025-07-10T11:11:39.645095",
                "msl_citation": "Liu, J. (2022). <i>Permeability of bituminous coal to CH4 and CO2 under fixed volume and stress boundary conditions: Effects of sorption</i> (Version 1.0) [Data set]. Utrecht University. https://doi.org/10.24416/UU01-XOJCFK",
                "msl_datacite_version": "Version 1.0",
                "msl_description_abstract": "We report permeability data of a cylindrical sample of high volatile bituminous coal (25mm in diameter) with a clearly visible cleat system, to CH4 and CO2, performed under (near) fixed volume versus fixed stress conditions. To isolate the effect of sorption on permeability evolution, helium (non-sorbing gas) was used as a control fluid. All flow-through tests reported here were conducted under conditions of single-phase flow at 40℃, employing Terzaghi effective stresses of 14-35MPa. This experimental study aimed to gain a better understanding of the effects of fully coupled stress-strain-sorption-diffusion behaviour on permeability evolution in coal reservoirs during CO2-Enhanced Coalbed Methane (ECBM) recovery. Our results obtained permeability evolution versus changes in effective stress under both fixed volume and fixed stress conditions, showing an exponential correlation. Importantly, permeability (κ) obtained at similar effective stresses showed κ_helium > κ_(CH_4 ) >> κ_(CO_2 ), and κ measured at fixed volume is higher than fixed stress. This all demonstrates that permeability to CH4 and CO2, under in-situ boundary conditions, is strongly influenced by the coupled effects of a) self-stress generated by swelling, b) the change in effective stress coefficient upon sorption, c) sorption-induced closure of transport paths independently of poro-elastic effect, and d) heterogeneous gas penetration and equilibration, dependent on diffusion. Our results also show that the Walsh permeability model offers a promising basis for relating permeability evolution to in-situ stress evolution, using appropriate parameter values corrected for the effects of stress-strain-sorption-diffusion. These data are supplementary to: \nLiu, J., Spiers, C.J., 2022. Permeability of bituminous coal to CH4 and CO2 under fixed volume and stress boundary conditions: Effects of sorption. Submitted to Frontiers in Earth Sciences. ",
                "msl_description_abstract_annotated": "We report <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/rockphysics/1.3/measured_property-permeability\"]'>permeability</span> data of a cylindrical sample of high volatile <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/materials/1.3/sedimentary_rock-coal-bituminous_coal\"]'>bituminous coal</span> (25mm in diameter) with a clearly visible cleat system, to CH4 and <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/geochemistry/1.3/measured_property-carbon_c-carbon_dioxide\"]'>CO2,</span> performed under (near) fixed volume versus fixed stress conditions. To isolate the effect of sorption on <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/rockphysics/1.3/measured_property-permeability\"]'>permeability</span> evolution, <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/geochemistry/1.3/measured_property-helium\"]'>helium</span> (non-sorbing gas) was used as a control fluid. All flow-through tests reported here were conducted under conditions of single-phase flow at 40℃, employing Terzaghi effective stresses of 14-35MPa. This experimental study aimed to gain a better understanding of the effects of fully coupled stress-<span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/rockphysics/1.3/measured_property-strain\", \"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/analoguemodelling/1.3/measured_property-strain\"]'>strain</span>-sorption-diffusion behaviour on <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/rockphysics/1.3/measured_property-permeability\"]'>permeability</span> evolution in <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/materials/1.3/sedimentary_rock-coal\"]'>coal</span> reservoirs during CO2-Enhanced Coalbed <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/geochemistry/1.3/measured_property-carbon_c-methane\"]'>Methane</span> (ECBM) recovery. Our results obtained <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/rockphysics/1.3/measured_property-permeability\"]'>permeability</span> evolution versus changes in effective stress under both fixed volume and fixed stress conditions, showing an exponential correlation. Importantly, <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/rockphysics/1.3/measured_property-permeability\"]'>permeability</span> (κ) obtained at similar effective stresses showed κ_helium > κ_(CH_4 ) >> κ_(CO_2 ), and κ measured at fixed volume is higher than fixed stress. This all demonstrates that <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/rockphysics/1.3/measured_property-permeability\"]'>permeability</span> to CH4 and <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/geochemistry/1.3/measured_property-carbon_c-carbon_dioxide\"]'>CO2,</span> under in-situ boundary conditions, is strongly influenced by the coupled effects of a) self-stress generated by swelling, b) the change in effective stress coefficient upon sorption, c) sorption-induced closure of transport paths independently of <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/rockphysics/1.3/inferred_deformation_behavior-deformation_behaviour-poroelastic_deformation\"]'>poro-elastic</span> effect, and d) heterogeneous gas penetration and equilibration, dependent on diffusion. Our results also show that the Walsh <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/rockphysics/1.3/measured_property-permeability\"]'>permeability</span> model offers a promising basis for relating <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/rockphysics/1.3/measured_property-permeability\"]'>permeability</span> evolution to in-situ stress evolution, using appropriate parameter values corrected for the effects of stress-<span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/rockphysics/1.3/measured_property-strain\", \"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/analoguemodelling/1.3/measured_property-strain\"]'>strain</span>-sorption-diffusion. These data are supplementary to: \nLiu, J., Spiers, C.J., 2022. <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/rockphysics/1.3/measured_property-permeability\"]'>Permeability</span> of <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/materials/1.3/sedimentary_rock-coal-bituminous_coal\"]'>bituminous coal</span> to CH4 and CO2 under fixed volume and stress boundary conditions: Effects of sorption. Submitted to Frontiers in Earth Sciences. ",

                "msl_citation": "D'Acquisto, M. (2022). <i>Model output for the paper \"On the cause of enhanced landward motion of the overriding plate after a major subduction earthquake\"</i> (Version 1.0) [Data set]. Utrecht University. https://doi.org/10.24416/UU01-D7MWAP",
                "msl_datacite_version": "1.0",
                "msl_description_abstract": "This repository contains the relevant data (part of numerical model output) used to plot the figures in the main body of the manuscript entitled \"On the cause of enhanced landward motion of the overriding plate after a major subduction earthquake\", by Mario D'Acquisto, Matthew Herman, Riccardo Riva, and Rob Govers, submitted for publication in Journal of Geophysical Research: Solid Earth.\n\nPaper abstract: \"Greater landward velocities were recorded after 6 megathrust earthquakes in subduction zone regions adjacent to the ruptured portion. Previous explanations invoked either increased slip deficit accumulation or plate bending during postseismic relaxation, with different implications for seismic hazard. We investigate whether bending can be expected to reproduce this observed enhanced landward motion (ELM). We use 3D quasi-dynamic finite element models with periodic earthquakes. We find that afterslip downdip of the brittle megathrust exclusively produces enhanced trenchward surface motion in the overriding plate. Viscous relaxation produces ELM when a depth limit is imposed on afterslip. This landward motion results primarily from in-plane elastic bending of the overriding plate due to trenchward viscous flow in the mantle wedge near the rupture. Modeled ELM is, however, incompatible with the observations, which are an order of magnitude greater and last longer after the earthquake. Varying mantle viscosity, plate elasticity, maximum afterslip depth, earthquake size, and megathrust locking outside of the rupture does not significantly change this conclusion. The observed ELM consequently appears to reflect faster slip deficit accumulation, implying a greater seismic hazard in lateral segments of the subduction zone.\"\n\nThe model consists of a three-dimensional (3D) finite element method (FEM) simulation of the megathrust earthquake cycle with two fully elastic plates and Maxwell viscoelastic mantle.\n\nThe software used to perform the simulations and extract the model output in the files stored here was GTECTON (Govers & Wortel, 1993, 2005; Govers et al., 2018), version 2021.0. The software used to generate the relevant figures in the paper from the data was Generic Mapping Tools (GMT) (Wessel et al., 2019) version 6.3.0.\n\nEach directory corresponds to a different model. The meaning of each model name, as well as the meaning of the file name and the internal data format of the files, are specified in the readme file (readme.txt). All files are plain text files.\n\nFor more information regarding the goals, model features, and output, please refer to the paper.\n\nContact person: Mario D'Acquisto - m.dacquisto@uu.nl",
                "msl_description_abstract_annotated": "This repository contains the relevant data (part of numerical model output) used to plot the figures in the main body of the manuscript entitled \"On the cause of enhanced landward motion of the overriding plate after a major <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/geologicalsetting/1.3/tectonic_plate_boundary-convergent_tectonic_plate_boundary-subduction\"]'>subduction</span> earthquake\", by Mario D'Acquisto, Matthew Herman, Riccardo Riva, and Rob Govers, submitted for publication in Journal of Geophysical Research: Solid Earth.\n\nPaper abstract: \"Greater landward velocities were recorded after 6 <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/geologicalsetting/1.3/tectonic_plate_boundary-convergent_tectonic_plate_boundary-subduction-subducting_plate_interface\", \"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/geologicalsetting/1.3/tectonic_deformation_structure-tectonic_fault-thrust_fault\"]'>megathrust</span> earthquakes in <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/geologicalsetting/1.3/tectonic_plate_boundary-convergent_tectonic_plate_boundary-subduction\"]'>subduction zone</span> regions adjacent to the ruptured portion. Previous explanations invoked either increased slip deficit accumulation or plate bending during postseismic <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/rockphysics/1.3/measured_property-stress_relaxation\"]'>relaxation</span>, with different implications for seismic hazard. We investigate whether bending can be expected to reproduce this observed enhanced landward motion (ELM). We use 3D quasi-dynamic finite element models with periodic earthquakes. We find that afterslip downdip of the brittle <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/geologicalsetting/1.3/tectonic_plate_boundary-convergent_tectonic_plate_boundary-subduction-subducting_plate_interface\", \"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/geologicalsetting/1.3/tectonic_deformation_structure-tectonic_fault-thrust_fault\"]'>megathrust</span> exclusively produces enhanced trenchward surface motion in the overriding plate. Viscous <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/rockphysics/1.3/measured_property-stress_relaxation\"]'>relaxation</span> produces ELM when a depth limit is imposed on afterslip. This landward motion results primarily from in-plane elastic bending of the overriding plate due to trenchward viscous flow in the mantle <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/geologicalsetting/1.3/tectonic_plate_boundary-convergent_tectonic_plate_boundary-subduction-accretionary_wedge\"]'>wedge</span> near the rupture. Modeled ELM is, however, incompatible with the observations, which are an order of magnitude greater and last longer after the earthquake. Varying mantle <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/rockphysics/1.3/measured_property-viscosity\", \"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/analoguemodelling/1.3/measured_property-viscosity\"]'>viscosity</span>, plate <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/rockphysics/1.3/measured_property-elasticity\", \"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/analoguemodelling/1.3/measured_property-elasticity\"]'>elasticity</span>, maximum afterslip depth, earthquake size, and <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/geologicalsetting/1.3/tectonic_plate_boundary-convergent_tectonic_plate_boundary-subduction-subducting_plate_interface\", \"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/geologicalsetting/1.3/tectonic_deformation_structure-tectonic_fault-thrust_fault\"]'>megathrust</span> locking outside of the rupture does not significantly change this conclusion. The observed ELM consequently appears to reflect faster slip deficit accumulation, implying a greater seismic hazard in lateral segments of the <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/geologicalsetting/1.3/tectonic_plate_boundary-convergent_tectonic_plate_boundary-subduction\"]'>subduction zone</span>.\"\n\nThe model consists of a three-dimensional (3D) finite element method (FEM) simulation of the <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/geologicalsetting/1.3/tectonic_plate_boundary-convergent_tectonic_plate_boundary-subduction-subducting_plate_interface\", \"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/geologicalsetting/1.3/tectonic_deformation_structure-tectonic_fault-thrust_fault\"]'>megathrust</span> earthquake cycle with two fully elastic plates and Maxwell viscoelastic mantle.\n\nThe software used to perform the simulations and extract the model output in the files stored here was GTECTON (Govers & Wortel, 1993, 2005; Govers et al., 2018), version 2021.0. The software used to generate the relevant figures in the paper from the data was Generic Mapping Tools (GMT) (Wessel et al., 2019) version 6.3.0.\n\nEach directory corresponds to a different model. The meaning of each model name, as well as the meaning of the file name and the internal data format of the files, are specified in the readme file (readme.txt). All files are plain text files.\n\nFor more information regarding the goals, model features, and output, please refer to the paper.\n\nContact person: Mario D'Acquisto - m.dacquisto@uu.nl",

                "msl_citation": "D'Acquisto, M. (2022). <i>Model output for the paper \"Offshore landward motion shortly after a subduction earthquake implies rapid relocking of the shallow megathrust\"</i> (Version 1.0) [Data set]. Utrecht University. https://doi.org/10.24416/UU01-SS41UK",
                "msl_datacite_version": "1.0",
                "msl_description_abstract": "This repository contains the relevant data (part of numerical model output) used to plot the figures in the main body of the manuscript entitled \"Offshore landward motion shortly after a subduction earthquake implies rapid relocking of the shallow megathrust\", by Mario D'Acquisto and Rob Govers.\n\nPaper abstract: \"Geodetic observations after large subduction earthquakes reflect multiple postseismic processes, including megathrust relocking. What the timing of relocking is, and how well observations constrain it, is unclear. It has been inferred to explain some observed landward motion that occurs within months. It has also been considered unable to explain other, greater landward motion, including off the coast of Japan beginning weeks after the 2011 Tohoku earthquake, which is attributed to postseismic relaxation. We use generic, 3D numerical models to show that relocking, particularly of the shallow interface, is needed for postseismic relaxation to produce landward motion on the tip of the overriding plate. We argue that this finding is consistent with previous simulations that implicitly relock the megathrust where afterslip is not included, that the Tohoku megathrust thus relocked within less than two months of the earthquake, and that the shallow megathrust probably behaves as a true, unstably sliding asperity.\"\n\nThe model consists of a three-dimensional (3D) finite element method (FEM) simulation of the megathrust earthquake cycle with two fully elastic plates and Maxwell viscoelastic mantle.\n\nThe software used to perform the simulations and extract the model output in the files stored here was GTECTON (Govers & Wortel, 1993, 2005; Govers et al., 2018), version 2021.0. The software used to generate the relevant figures in the paper from the data was Generic Mapping Tools (GMT) (Wessel et al., 2019) version 6.4.0.\n\nEach directory corresponds to a different model. The meaning of each model name, as well as the meaning of the file name and the internal data format of the files, are specified in the readme file (readme.txt). All files are plain text files.\n\nFor more information regarding the goals, model features, and output, please refer to the paper.\n\nContact person: Mario D'Acquisto - m.dacquisto@uu.nl",
                "msl_description_abstract_annotated": "This repository contains the relevant data (part of numerical model output) used to plot the figures in the main body of the manuscript entitled \"Offshore landward motion shortly after a <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/geologicalsetting/1.3/tectonic_plate_boundary-convergent_tectonic_plate_boundary-subduction\"]'>subduction</span> earthquake implies rapid relocking of the shallow <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/geologicalsetting/1.3/tectonic_plate_boundary-convergent_tectonic_plate_boundary-subduction-subducting_plate_interface\", \"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/geologicalsetting/1.3/tectonic_deformation_structure-tectonic_fault-thrust_fault\"]'>megathrust</span>\", by Mario D'Acquisto and Rob Govers.\n\nPaper abstract: \"Geodetic observations after large <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/geologicalsetting/1.3/tectonic_plate_boundary-convergent_tectonic_plate_boundary-subduction\"]'>subduction</span> earthquakes reflect multiple postseismic processes, including <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/geologicalsetting/1.3/tectonic_plate_boundary-convergent_tectonic_plate_boundary-subduction-subducting_plate_interface\", \"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/geologicalsetting/1.3/tectonic_deformation_structure-tectonic_fault-thrust_fault\"]'>megathrust</span> relocking. It has also been considered unable to explain other, greater landward motion, including off the coast of Japan beginning weeks after the 2011 Tohoku earthquake, which is attributed to postseismic <span data-uris='[\"https://epos-msl.uu.nl/voc/rockphysics/1.3/measured_property-stress_relaxation\"]'>relaxation</span>.
